                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilizing fluorine to achieve high-voltage and ultra-stable Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Liang; Yu, Fu-Da; Xia, Yang; Jiang, Yun-Shan; Sui, Xu-Lei; Zhao, Lei; Meng, Xiang-Hui; Que, Lan-Fang; Wang, Zhen-Bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">82</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105659</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is a promising cathode candidate for sodium ion batteries due to its high working voltage.  However, an "unknown" low-voltage plateau around ∼3.3 V lowers its operating voltage and puzzles researchers.  Herein, the reasons for its appearance are explored.  It is found that the formation of the low-voltage plateau originates from the extra-generated [VO6] induced by the fluorine loss during the synthesis.  To enable better performance, a feasible strategy of stabilizing fluorine is proposed to eliminate the low-voltage plateau.  It is demonstrated that this strategy can effectively guarantee the existence of fluorine and modulate the local electronic structure of V to maintain [VO4F2] in Na3V2(PO4)2F3 phase, thus eliminating the undesirable plateau and achieving an operating-voltage increase of ∼100 mV.  Moreover, the enhanced structural stability and kinetics of the optimized Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode are confirmed by in-situ XRD.  As expected, the Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode delivers higher energy d. (446.4 Wh kg-1), better rate capability and longer cycling performance (89.2%@30 C after 1000 cycles).  Furthermore, its excellent adaptability to wide temp. range (-25 °C-55 °C) and strong competence in Na3V2(PO4)2F3||hard carbon full-cell are verified.  These excellent properties further qualifyNa3V2(PO4)2F3 as a competitive cathode for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202201719"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synergistic Effect, Structural and Morphology Evolution, and Doping Mechanism of Spherical Br-Doped Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>/C toward Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2201719</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202201719</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D18%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2201719%26journal%3DSmall%26issue%3D22%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DR.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BFan%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DP.%2BGao%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BHan%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26title%3DSynergistic%2BEffect%252C%2BStructural%2Band%2BMorphology%2BEvolution%252C%2Band%2BDoping%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BSpherical%2BBr-Doped%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%252FC%2Btoward%2BEnhanced%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.202201719&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.4c00702&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.202201719&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic Effect, Structural and Morphology Evolution, and Doping Mechanism of Spherical Br-Doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C toward Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhuang; Zhang, Ruijie; Fan, Changling; Liu, Xunlin; Gao, Peng; Zhang, Weihua; Liu, Zhixiao; Han, Shaochang; Liu, Jinshui; Liu, Jilei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2201719</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 has attracted wide attention due to its high voltage platform, and stable crystal structure.  However, its application is limited by the low electronic cond. and the ease formation of impurity.  In this paper, the spherical Br-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C is successfully obtained by a one-step spray drying technol.  The hard template polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) supplements the loss of fluorine, forming porous structure that accelerates the infiltration of electrolyte.  The soft template cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) enables doping of bromine and can also control the fluorine content, meanwhile, the self-assembly effect strengthens the structure and refines the size of spherical particles.  The loss, compensation, and regulation mechanism of fluorine are investigated.  The Br-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C sphere exhibits superior rate capability with the capacities of 116.1, 105.1, and 95.2 mAh g-1 at 1, 10, and 30 C, and excellent cyclic performance with 98.3% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 10 C.  The d. functional theory (DFT) calcn. shows weakened charge localization and enhanced cond., meanwhile the diffusion energy barrier of sodium ions is reduced with Br doping. (-15°C vs 30°C), triggers the exploration of its structural origins with a surprising finding that the migratable nature of vanadium in NVCP leads to detrimental structural degrdn. of the polyanionic host upon cycling.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">VSC-doping and VSU-doping of Na3V2-xTix(PO4)2F3 compounds for sodium ion battery cathodes: Analysis of electrochemical performance and kinetic properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Hongming; Ling, Moxiang; Xu, Wenbin; Li, Xianfeng; Zheng, Qiong; Zhang, Huamin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ion doping strategy is employed to improve the rate performance of insulated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) as cathode of sodium ion batteries.  The concepts of VSU-doping (the valence state of the doping ion keeps unchanged during the synthesis) and VSC-doping (the valence state changes during the synthesis) have been introduced in this research.  Titanium with different valence states (Ti2+, Ti3+, Ti4+) is selected as the doping element to investigate the VSU-doping and VSC-doping effects on NVPF for the first time.  Based on a series of characterizations, it is verified that a moderate Ti doping is able to effectively improve the rate performance of NVPF through the enhancing of electron conduction and sodium ion diffusion, and the advantage is more obvious for the VSC-doping samples.  Among all the NVPF-Tix+0.1 (x = 2, 3, 4) samples, the NVPF-Ti2+0.1 treated with a VSC-doping (Ti source: TiO) possesses the min. particle size distribution (∼40 nm), exhibits the highest initial specific capacity of 125 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C, and a very high rate capability (104 mA h g-1 at 40 C, 81 mA h g-1 at 80 C, 41 mA h g-1 at 200 C) as well, which has surpassed most of the reported results.  When coupling with Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) as the anode, the NVPF-Ti2+0.1-NVP pseudo-sym. full cell shows a high initial specific capacity of 99.6 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C and an outstanding rate capability (60% of initial specific capacity at 40 C).  Subsequently, a detailed investigation on the effects of the VSU-doping and VSC-doping processes on the battery performance, in combination with DFT calcns. and anal. of kinetic properties, has been conducted, esp. from the perspective of electron conduction and sodium ion diffusion.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1149/2.015209jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, S.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanion-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni Qiao; Bai Ying; Wu Feng; Wu Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries, representative members of the post-lithium-battery club, are very attractive and promising for large-scale energy storage applications.  The increasing technological improvements in sodium-ion batteries (Na-ion batteries) are being driven by the demand for Na-based electrode materials that are resource-abundant, cost-effective, and long lasting.  Polyanion-type compounds are among the most promising electrode materials for Na-ion batteries due to their stability, safety, and suitable operating voltages.  The most representative polyanion-type electrode materials are Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaTi2(PO4)3 for Na-based cathode and anode materials, respectively.  Both show superior electrochemical properties and attractive prospects in terms of their development and application in Na-ion batteries.  Carbonophosphate Na3MnCO3PO4 and amorphous FePO4 have also recently emerged and are contributing to further developing the research scope of polyanion-type Na-ion batteries.  However, the typical low conductivity and relatively low capacity performance of such materials still restrict their development.  This paper presents a brief review of the research progress of polyanion-type electrode materials for Na-ion batteries, summarizing recent accomplishments, highlighting emerging strategies, and discussing the remaining challenges of such systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.09.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High capacity-favorable tap density cathode material based on three-dimensional carbonous framework supported Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C@RGO (NVPF/C@RGO) composites with interconnected 3D carbonous framework are composed of NVPF nanoparticles, coating layer of amorphous carbon and RGO nanosheets, where the RGO serves as the main framework.  The low carbon content (4.6%) and uniform NVPF nanoparticles supported by the unique 3D carbonous architecture lead to low sp. surface area and favorable tap d.  By taking full advantage of the interconnected 3D carbonous framework, the excellent electronic cond. of NVPF/C@RGO is three orders of magnitude higher than that of pristine NVPF/C, resulting in favorable enhanced electrochem. performance.  The initial capacity of 124.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C-rate and a high discharge capacity of 119.2 mAh g-1 with an excellent retention of 90.9% after 700 cycles at 1 C can be attained.  Most importantly, NVPF nanoparticles connected with 3D carbonous framework have a low sp. surface area, favorable tap d., simple tech. procedure, and show great potential to optimize battery performance, apply in large scale energy storage and extend to all polyanion-based cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.cclet.2022.107978"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research progress on Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>-based cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chin.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Impact of Electrolyte Additives and Upper Cut-off Voltage on the Formation of a Rock salt Surface Layer in LiNi0.8Mn0.1Co0.1O2 Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jing; Liu, Hanshuo; Xia, Jian; Cameron, Andrew R.; Nie, Mengyun; Botton, Gianluigi A.; Dahn, J. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">164</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A655-A665</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Many literature reports show that layered Li-Ni-Mn-Co oxides (NMC) have a surface reconstruction to a rock salt (Fm3m) structure which is claimed to be responsible for the increase in cell impedance during high voltage cycling.  It is important to det. if appropriate electrolyte additives can suppress the surface reconstructions of NMC materials.  LiNi0.8Mn0.1Co0.1O2 (NMC811)/Graphite pouch cells with different electrolyte additives and different upper cutoff potentials were charge-discharge cycled and the electrodes were recovered for z-contrast scanning transmission electron microscope (STEM) studies.  It was found that there was no significant surface layer growth for cells cycled between 2.8-4.1 V.  For cells with an upper cutoff voltage of 4.3 V, the electrodes from cells with control electrolyte (no additives) showed the thickest surface layer.  The electrolyte additives vinylene carbonate (VC) and prop-1-ene-1,3-sultone (PES) were found to suppress the growth of the surface layer.  However, cells with PES showed a more rapid capacity fade than control cells or cells with 2% VC showing that, at least for NMC811/graphite cells with PES or VC additives, failure cannot only be solely ascribed to a growing rock salt surface layer.  Other processes, for example assocd. with electrolyte oxidn., are believed to be responsible for failure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.10.065"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tornheim, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharifi-Asl, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Garcia, J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of electrolyte composition on rock salt surface degradation in NMC cathodes during high-voltage potentiostatic holds</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tornheim, Adam; Sharifi-Asl, Soroosh; Garcia, Juan C.; Bareno, Javier; Iddir, Hakim; Shahbazian-Yassar, Reza; Zhang, Zhengcheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">216-225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Surface degrdn. of lithium-ion cathodes at high voltages represents a significant barrier to increasing the useable energy of conventional cathodes.  Though much work has been focused on mitigating the detrimental effects of such phenomena, the complex and correlated mechanisms involved have made progress difficult.  Herein, the effect of electrolyte identity on surface degrdn. is examd.  LiNi0.5Mn0.3Co0.2O2 (NMC532)/Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) full cells were constructed using three different electrolytes: a baseline org. carbonate electrolyte, a baseline org. carbonate electrolyte with an oxidizable additive, and a fluorinated carbonate electrolyte.  Each system was subjected to a 60 h potentiostatic hold at 3.05 V (4.6 V vs. Li+/Li) and subsequently deconstructed for characterization via transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and electron energy loss spectroscopy (EELS).  Mol. simulations were carried out on each distinct component of the three electrolytes in contact with crystal surfaces of an NMC532 particle.  Results indicate an affinity for the additive-contg. electrolyte to ext. at. oxygen from the cathode surface, whereas the fluorinated electrolyte components have negligible interactions.  Hydrogen abstraction from the baseline electrolyte is facilitated by the NMC532 surface.  TEM anal. of cathode surfaces, after the potentiostatic holds, revealed that the NMC532 particles cycled with the additive-contg. electrolyte underwent significant surface degrdn., including changes to local crystal structure in a region penetrating 20-40 nm from the surface; consistent with oxygen and lithium loss from the cathode material.  However, the NMC532 in contact with the fluorinated electrolyte showed a disordered layer of just a few nm in thickness, similar to the depth of crystal disorder obsd. in pristine NMC532 primary particles.  EELS data of the oxygen K-edge also indicated transition metal (TM) redn., consistent with oxygen loss and changes in crystal structure extending into the cathode surface for each of the electrolytes surveyed.  These surface reactions, including oxygen loss, are shown to correlate well with elevated oxidn. currents and surface reconstructions of cathode particles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201901431"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reeves, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Foix, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cometto, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mariyappan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Salanne, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A New Electrolyte Formulation for Securing High Temperature Cycling and Storage Performances of Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A New Electrolyte Formulation for Securing High Temperature Cycling and Storage Performances of Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Guochun; Reeves, Kyle; Foix, Dominique; Li, Zhujie; Cometto, Claudio; Mariyappan, Sathiya; Salanne, Mathieu; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na-ion battery is recognized as a possible alternative to the Li-ion battery for applications where power and cost override energy d. performance.  However, the increasing instability of their electrolyte with temp. is still problematic.  Thus, a central question remains how to design Na-based electrolytes.  The discovery of a Na-based electrolyte formulation is reported which enlists four additives (vinylene carbonate, succinonitrile, 1,3-propane sultone, and sodium difluoro(oxalate)borate) in proper quantities that synergistically combine their pos. attributes to enable a stable solid electrolyte interphase at both neg. and pos. electrodes surface at 55°C.  Moreover, the role of each additive that consists in producing specific NaF coatings, thin elastomers, sulfate-based deposits, and so on via combined impedance and XPS is rationalized.  It is demonstrated that empirical electrolyte design rules previously established for Li-ion technol. together with theor. guidance is vital in the quest for better Na-based electrolytes that can be extended to other chemistries.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Construction of Uniform and Robust Cathode-Electrolyte Interphase for Li-Rich Layered Oxides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jingteng; Liang, Yuan; Zhang, Xu; Zhang, Zihe; Wang, Errui; He, Shiman; Wang, Boya; Han, Zhijie; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Yu, Haijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-energy-d. Li-rich layered oxides (LLOs) as promising cathodes for Li-ion batteries suffer from the dissoln. of transition metals (esp. manganese) and severe side reactions in conventional electrolytes, which greatly deteriorate their electrochem. performance.  Herein, an in situ "anchoring + pouring" synergistic cathode-electrolyte interphase (CEI) construction is realized by using 1,3,6-hexanetricarbonitrile (HTCN) and tris(trimethylsilyl) phosphate (TMSP) electrolyte additives to alleviate the challenges of an LLO (Li1.13Mn0.517Ni0.256Co0.097O2).  HTCN with three nitrile groups can tightly anchor transition metals by coordinative interaction to form the CEI framework, and TMSP will electrochem. decomp. to reshape the CEI layer.  The uniform and robust in situ constructed CEI layer can suppress the transition metal dissoln., shield the cathode against diverse side reactions, and significantly improve the overall electrochem. performance of the cathod with a discharge voltage decay of only 0.5 mV cycle-1.  Further investigations based on a series of exptl. techniques and theor. calcns. have revealed the compn. of in situ constructed CEI layers and their distribution, including the enhanced HTCN anchoring effect after lattice densification of LLOs.  This study provides insights into the in situ CEI construction for enhancing the performance of high-energy and high-voltage cathode materials through effective, convenient, and economical electrolyte approaches.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.2c01100"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Toward High Temperature Sodium Metal Batteries via Regulating the Electrolyte/Electrode Interfacial Chemistries</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2032</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2042</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Toward High Temperature Sodium Metal Batteries via Regulating the Electrolyte/Electrode Interfacial Chemistries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Xueying; Cao, Zhang; Gu, Zhenyi; Huang, Liqiang; Sun, Zhonghui; Zhao, Tong; Yu, Sijie; Wu, Xing-Long; Luo, Wei; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries based on sodium metal anodes (SMAs) are endowed with much higher energy d. than traditional sodium-ion batteries.  However, the use of SMAs brings intrinsic challenges of dendrite growth and unstable solid/electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation.  This situation can be further exacerbated at high temp. (&gt;55°C, HT).  Here, we resolve such "HT-challenge" by formulating a thermally stable sulfolane (SL)-based electrolyte that regulates the electrode/electrolyte interfacial chemistries.  Besides rapid Na anode passivation enabled by fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) mols., a nitrile-based 1,3,6-hexanetricarbonitrile (HTCN) cosolvent is simultaneously introduced, whose three electron-rich -C≃ N groups interact with the electropos. metal ions of Na3V2(PO4)2O2F, shielding away solvent attacks occurring at the cathode interface. Even at 80°C, the cell still delivers ~ 89.1% of its initial capacity after 100 cycles, whereas the control sample fails rapidly within 30 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.06.075"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1,3,6-Hexanetricarbonitrile as electrolyte additive for enhancing electrochemical performance of high voltage Li-rich layered oxide cathode</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">1,3,6-Hexanetricarbonitrile (HTN) was investigated as an electrolyte additive to improve the electrochem. performance of the Li1.2Ni0.13Co0.13Mn0.54O2 cathode at high operating voltage (4.8 V).  Linear sweep voltammetry (LSV) results indicate that HTN can improve the oxidn. potential of the electrolyte.  The influences of HTN on the electrochem. behaviors and surface properties of the cathode at high voltage were investigated by galvanostatic charge/discharge test, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), and ex-situ phys. characterizations.  Charge-discharge results demonstrate that the capacity retention of the Li1.2Ni0.13Co0.13Mn0.54O2 cathode in 1% HTN-contg. electrolyte after 150 cycles at 0.5 C is improved to 92.3%, which is much higher than that in the std. electrolyte (ED).                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding How Nitriles Stabilize Electrolyte/Electrode Interface at High Voltage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhi, Huozhen; Xing, Lidan; Zheng, Xiongwen; Xu, Kang; Li, Weishan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitriles have received extensive attention for their unique ability in stabilizing electrolytes against oxidn. at high voltages.  It was generally believed that their anodic stability originates from a monolayer of chemisorbed nitrile mols. on transition-metal oxide surface, which phys. expels carbonate mols. and prevents their oxidative decompn.  We overturn this belief based on calcn. and exptl. results and demonstrate that, like many high voltage film-forming electrolyte additives, nitriles also experience an oxidative decompn. at high voltages, and the high oxidn. stability of nitrile-contg. electrolytes is merely the consequence of a new interphasial chem.  This important mechanistic correction would be of high significance in guiding the design of new electrolytes and interphases for the future battery chemistries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/sia.6744"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Succinonitrile as a high-voltage additive in the electrolyte of LiNi<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.3</sub>O<sub>2</sub>/graphite full batteries</span>. <i>Surf.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Succinonitrile as a high-voltage additive in the electrolyte of LiNi0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2/graphite full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Songyi; Liu, Yan; Zhang, Hong; Fan, Chaojun; Fan, Weizhen; Yu, Le; Du, Xueyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Surface and Interface Analysis</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">52</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">364-373</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a functional additive, succinonitrile (SN) can be used in LiNi0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2/graphite lithium ion batteries to broaden the oxidn. electrochem. window of the electrolyte and significantly improve its rate performance and high-voltage cycle performance.  Linear sweep voltammetry (LSV) shows that EC/EMC-based electrolytes with SN have higher oxidn. potentials (approx. 6.1 V vs Li/Li+).  The capacity retention of LiNi0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2/graphite full cell with 0.5-wt% SN added to the electrolyte and 120 cycles between 2.75 and 4.4 V was significantly increased from 67.96% to 84.0%.  It is indicated that the LiNi0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2 (NCM523) battery contg. 0.5-wt% SN-based electrolyte has better cycleability and capacity retention at high cutoff voltage.  In addn., electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), SEM (SEM), and XPS of the full cell were used to characterize the effect of SN on the cell.  It is proved that the SN participates in the interfacial reaction between the electrode and the electrolyte to form a stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer, thereby effectively suppressing the increase of the charge transfer resistance and reducing the elution of the transition metal cations.  These results indicate that SN can be used as a functional additive for high-voltage lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202310051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Z.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Engineering with Tamed Electrode Interphases for High-Voltage Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrolyte design has become ever more important to enhance the performance of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the flammability issue and high reactivity of the conventional electrolytes remain a major problem, esp. when the LIBs are operated at high voltage and extreme temps.  Herein, we design a novel non-flammable fluorinated ester electrolyte that enables high cycling stability in wide-temp. variations (e.g., -50 °C-60 °C) and superior power capability (fast charge rates up to 5.0 C) for the graphite||LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 (NCM811) battery at high voltage (i.e., &gt;4.3 V vs. Li/Li+). By elucidating the fundamental relationship between the Li+ solvation structure and electrochem. performance, we can facilitate the development of high-safety and high-energy-d. batteries operating in harsh conditions.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-021-00780-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ci, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Safe and Stable Lithium Metal Batteries Enabled by an Amide-Based Electrolyte</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">44</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Progress in nitrile-based polymer electrolytes for high performance lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Pu; Chai, Jingchao; Duan, Yulong; Liu, Zhihong; Cui, Guanglei; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Nitrile or cyano-based compds. have aroused interest in high performance battery electrolyte fields due to their unique characteristics such as a high dielec. const., high anodic oxidization potential and favorable interaction with lithium ions.  Particularly, owing to the presence of a unique plastic-cryst. phase, succinonitrile/salt-based solid electrolytes possess an ultra high ionic cond. of more than 10-3 S cm-1 at room temp.  Herein, recent progress in nitrile-based polymer electrolytes has been reviewed in terms of their potential application in flexible, solid-state or high voltage lithium batteries.  Factors affecting the ionic cond. of nitrile-based electrolytes have also been summarized.  We hope that fresh and established researchers can obtain a clear perspective of nitrile based polymer electrolytes and our mini review can spur more extensive interest for the exploration of high performance batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C9CP01839E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ugata, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thomas, M. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mandai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ueno, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dokko, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Watanabe, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Li-ion hopping conduction in highly concentrated lithium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide/dinitrile liquid electrolytes</span>. <i>Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>21</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">19</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">9759</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9768</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C9CP01839E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D21%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D9759-9768%26journal%3DPhys.%2BChem.%2BChem.%2BPhys.%26issue%3D19%26author%3DY.%2BUgata%26author%3DM.%2BL.%2BThomas%26author%3DT.%2BMandai%26author%3DK.%2BUeno%26author%3DK.%2BDokko%26author%3DM.%2BWatanabe%26title%3DLi-ion%2Bhopping%2Bconduction%2Bin%2Bhighly%2Bconcentrated%2Blithium%2Bbis%2528fluorosulfonyl%2529amide%252Fdinitrile%2Bliquid%2Belectrolytes%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC9CP01839E&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.4c00702&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC9CP01839E&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li-ion hopping conduction in highly concentrated lithium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide/dinitrile liquid electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ugata, Yosuke; Thomas, Morgan L.; Mandai, Toshihiko; Ueno, Kazuhide; Dokko, Kaoru; Watanabe, Masayoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9759-9768</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li+ ion hopping conduction in highly concd. solns. of lithium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide (LiFSA) dissolved in dinitrile solvents, namely succinonitrile, glutaronitrile, and adiponitrile, was investigated.  Phase behaviors of the LiFSA/dinitrile binary mixts. assessed by differential scanning calorimetry suggested that LiFSA and the dinitriles form stable solvates in a molar ratio of 1 : 2.  For succinonitrile, a glass forming room temp. liq. is formed when [LiFSA]/[succinonitrile] &gt; 1.  The corresponding glutaronitrile and adiponitrile mixts. have m.ps. below 60°.  The self-diffusion coeffs. of Li+, FSA-, and dinitrile measured with pulsed field gradient NMR suggested that Li+ ion diffuses faster than anion and dinitrile in the liqs. of compn. [LiFSA]/[dinitrile] = 1/0.8, indicating emergence of Li+ ion hopping conduction.  X-ray crystallog. for the LiFSA-(dinitrile)2 solvates and Raman spectroscopy for the liqs. with compn. [LiFSA]/[dinitrile] &gt; 1 revealed that the two cyano groups of the dinitrile coordinate to two different Li+ ions and form solvent-bridged structures of (Li+-dinitrile-Li+).  In addn., the Raman spectra suggested that ionic aggregates (Li+-FSA--Li+) are formed in the liqs. with compn. [LiFSA]/[dinitrile] &gt; 1.  Although there is frequent ligand (dinitrile and/or anion) exchange for each Li+ ion in the liq. state, the polymeric network structures (solvent-bridged structure and ionic aggregates) restrict the facile motion of ligands because each ligand is interacting with multiple Li+ ions in the highly concd. electrolytes.  This induces the faster diffusion of the Li+ ion than that of the ligands, i.e., hopping conduction of Li+ through ligand exchange.  Electrochem. measurements clarified that the [LiFSA]/[succinonitrile] = 1/0.8 electrolyte possesses a relatively high Li+ transport ability (limiting c.d. &gt; 7 mA cm-2) thanks to the Li+ hopping conduction, regardless of its extremely high viscosity (3142 mPa s) and relatively low cond. (0.26 mS cm-1) at room temp.  Furthermore, this electrolyte was shown to have a high Li+ transference no. (&gt; 0.6), exhibited reversible Li metal deposition/dissoln. i.e. suppression of reductive decompn. of the solvent, and could be successfully applied to graphite and LiNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 half-cells.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.9b02129"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Verdier, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lepage, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zidani, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prébé, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aymé-Perrot, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pellerin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dollé, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rochefort, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cross-Linked Polyacrylonitrile-Based Elastomer Used as Gel Polymer Electrolyte in Li-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsaem.9b02129</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1099-1110%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DN.%2BVerdier%26author%3DD.%2BLepage%26author%3DR.%2BZidani%26author%3DA.%2BPr%25C3%25A9b%25C3%25A9%26author%3DD.%2BAym%25C3%25A9-Perrot%26author%3DC.%2BPellerin%26author%3DM.%2BDoll%25C3%25A9%26author%3DD.%2BRochefort%26title%3DCross-Linked%2BPolyacrylonitrile-Based%2BElastomer%2BUsed%2Bas%2BGel%2BPolymer%2BElectrolyte%2Bin%2BLi-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsaem.9b02129&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.4c00702&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsaem.9b02129&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cross-Linked Polyacrylonitrile-Based Elastomer Used as Gel Polymer Electrolyte in Li-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Verdier, Nina; Lepage, David; Zidani, Ramzi; Prebe, Arnaud; Ayme-Perrot, David; Pellerin, Christian; Dolle, Mickael; Rochefort, Dominic</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1099-1110</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0962</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Gel polymer electrolytes (GPEs) based on polyacrylonitrile elastomer (HNBR) are investigated for lithium-ion batteries application.  This study examines the acrylonitrile content, as well as the solvent used to make the GPE, to understand their impact on lithium solvation.  To do so, we propose a three-component system comprising HNBR:solvent:LiTFSI to pinpoint the correct ratio to provide the GPE with competitive cond.  IR spectroscopy is used to shed light on the interactions between nitriles and lithium ions.  Spin-lattice relaxation times (T1) and diffusion coeffs. of 7Li and 19F for various HNBR-based GPEs are obtained through PFG-NMR, enabling detn. of the transport no. of lithium cations (t+) and activation energy (Ea).  Among the GPEs tested, those composed of propylene carbonate with 2 M LiTFSI and HNBR with an acrylonitrile content of 50% are the most promising, with an ionic cond. of 2.1 × 10-3 S/cm, D7Li of 12.0 × 10-8 cm/s, and a t+ of 0.42 at room temp.  When this GPE was tested in Li5Ti4O12/LiFePO4 coin cells, a capacity of 135 mAh/g was obtained at a discharge rate of D/5, showing promising results for its use in Li-ion batteries.  This study highlights the benefits of high acrylonitrile content in the polymer and a solvent with a moderate donor no. to promote interactions between nitriles and Li+.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2021.106298"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, C.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Regulating lithium deposition via electropolymerization of acrylonitrile in rechargeable lithium metal batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>88</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">106298</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2021.106298</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D88%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D106298%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BShi%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BWen%26author%3DC.-C.%2BSu%26author%3DJ.%2BWu%26author%3DJ.%2BGuo%26title%3DRegulating%2Blithium%2Bdeposition%2Bvia%2Belectropolymerization%2Bof%2Bacrylonitrile%2Bin%2Brechargeable%2Blithium%2Bmetal%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2021.106298&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.4c00702&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2021.106298&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Regulating lithium deposition via electropolymerization of acrylonitrile in rechargeable lithium metal batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jian; Zhou, Musen; Shi, Jiayan; Zhao, Yifan; Wen, Xiaoyu; Su, Chi-Cheung; Wu, Jianzhong; Guo, Juchen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">88</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">106298</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report acrylonitrile (AN) as an effective additive in carbonate-based electrolytes to enable uniform and dense lithium (Li) deposition and to improve the coulombic efficiency of Li metal anode.  Our electrochem., spectroscopic, and theor. study reveal that AN is cathodically electropolymd. on the Li surface prior to the electrochem. decompn. of the electrolyte during Li deposition.  The resultant polyacrylonitrile artificial solid electrolyte interphase enables uniform nucleation and growth of Li deposition with significantly reduced side reactions.  The effectiveness of the AN additive is demonstrated in 0.4 Ah Li||LiNi0.6Mn0.2Co0.2O2 pouch cells (using 50-μm Li anode, 3 mAh cm-2 cathode areal capacity, and 4 g Ah-1 electrolyte) with excellent cycle stability under realistic charge-discharge condition.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201909887"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, J.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Toward Critical Electrode/Electrolyte Interfaces in Rechargeable Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">23</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1909887</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201909887</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D30%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1909887%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D23%26author%3DC.%2BYan%26author%3DR.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BXiao%26author%3DJ.-F.%2BDing%26author%3DL.%2BXu%26author%3DB.-Q.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.-Q.%2BHuang%26title%3DToward%2BCritical%2BElectrode%252FElectrolyte%2BInterfaces%2Bin%2BRechargeable%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201909887&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.4c00702&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201909887&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Toward Critical Electrode/Electrolyte Interfaces in Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Chong; Xu, Rui; Xiao, Ye; Ding, Jun-Fan; Xu, Lei; Li, Bo-Quan; Huang, Jia-Qi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1909887</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The electrode/electrolyte interface plays a crit. role in stabilizing the cycling performance and prolonging the service life of rechargeable batteries to meet the sustainable energy requirements of the mobile society.  The understanding of interfaces is still at the preliminary stage due to the limited research techniques and variable properties with time and potential.  Herein, the latest developments focused on the interfaces in rechargeable systems including the cathode electrolyte interphase (CEI) and solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) are reviewed.  The possible formation mechanisms of the electrode/electrolyte interface are discussed, followed by the introduction of two key affecting factors, specific adsorption and solvated coordinate structure, which will dominate the formation of the interface.  Finally, the structure and chem. compn. of the interface as well as the possible transport mechanism of lithium ions in the interface and the strategies to regulate the pathway through the interface are presented in detail.  This work sheds light on the fundamental understanding of the interface and provides rational scientific principles in designing the electrode/electrolyte interface and inspires the rational design of long-term cycling rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201803049"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Performance Sodium Metal Anodes Enabled by a Bifunctional Potassium Salt</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sodium Metal Anodes Enabled by a Bifunctional Potassium Salt</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Qiuwei; Zhong, Yiren; Wu, Min; Wang, Hongzhi; Wang, Hailiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9069-9072</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing Na metal anodes that can be deeply cycled with high efficiency for a long time is a prerequisite for rechargeable Na metal batteries to be practically useful despite their notable advantages in theor. energy d. and potential low cost.  Their high chem. reactivity with the electrolyte and tendency for dendrite formation are two major issues limiting the reversibility of Na metal electrodes.  In this work, we introduce for the first time potassium bis(trifluoromethylsulfonyl)imide (KTFSI) as a bifunctional electrolyte additive to stabilize Na metal electrodes, in which the TFSI- anions decomp. into lithium nitride and oxynitrides to render a desirable solid electrolyte interphase layer while the K+ cations preferentially adsorb onto Na protrusions and provide electrostatic shielding to suppress dendritic deposition.  Through the cooperation of the cations and anions, we have realized Na metal electrodes that can be deeply cycled at a capacity of 10 mAh cm-2 for hundreds of hours.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202208705"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interface Modulation of Metal Sulfide Anodes for Long-Cycle-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b09835"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">de
la Llave, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Borgel, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hartmann, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chesneau, F.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aurbach, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparison between Na-Ion and Li-Ion Cells: Understanding the Critical Role of the Cathodes Stability and the Anodes Pretreatment on the Cells Behavior</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsami.5b09835</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison between Na-Ion and Li-Ion Cells: Understanding the Critical Role of the Cathodes Stability and the Anodes Pretreatment on the Cells Behavior</span></div><div class="casAuthors">de la Llave, Ezequiel; Borgel, Valentina; Park, Kang-Joon; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Sun, Yang-Kook; Hartmann, Pascal; Chesneau, Frederick- Francois; Aurbach, Doron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. behavior of Na-ion and Li-ion full cells was investigated, using hard carbon as the anode material, and NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 and LiNi0.5Mn0.5O2 as the cathodes.  A detailed description of the structure, phase transition, electrochem. behavior and kinetics of the NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cathodes is presented, including interesting comparison with their lithium analog.  The crit. effect of the hard carbon anodes pretreatment in the total capacity and stability of full cells is clearly demonstrated.  Using impedance spectroscopy in three electrodes cells, we show that the full cell impedance is dominated by the contribution of the cathode side.  We discuss possible reasons for capacity fading of these systems, its connection to the cathode structure and relevant surface phenomena.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40811f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, K. T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">7</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2067</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2081</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ee40811f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Sung You; Kim, Youngjin; Park, Yuwon; Choi, Aram; Choi, Nam-Soon; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2067-2081</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  We discuss the similarities and dissimilarities of sodium- and lithium-ion batteries in terms of neg. and pos. electrodes.  Compared to the comprehensive body of work on lithium-ion batteries, research on sodium-ion batteries is still at the germination stage.  Since both sodium and lithium are alkali metals, they share similar chem. properties including ionicity, electronegativity and electrochem. reactivity.  They accordingly have comparable synthetic protocols and electrochem. performances, which indicates that sodium-ion batteries can be successfully developed based on previously applied approaches or methods in the lithium counterpart.  The electrode materials in Li-ion batteries provide the best library for research on Na-ion batteries because many Na-ion insertion hosts have their roots in Li-ion insertion hosts.  However, the larger size and different bonding characteristics of sodium ions influence the thermodn. and/or kinetic properties of sodium-ion batteries, which leads to unexpected behavior in electrochem. performance and reaction mechanism, compared to lithium-ion batteries.  This perspective provides a comparative overview of the major developments in the area of pos. and neg. electrode materials in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries in the past decade.  Highlighted are concepts in solid state chem. and electrochem. that have provided new opportunities for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1149/1.2756975"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barker, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gover, R. K. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Burns, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bryan, A. J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Li<sub>4/3</sub>Ti<sub>5/3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> || Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>: An Example of a Hybrid-Ion Cell Using a Non-graphitic Anode</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>154</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">A882</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, the sodium-ion battery is one of the hottest topics in the field of battery research.  For practical application, however, high tap d., which is a key point of electrode materials, has always been ignored in previous studies.  Here, we present the fabrication of a NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C/CNT composite cathode with a high tap d. of 1.2 g cm-3 for high power and long lifespan sodium-ion batteries.  The spherical NVPF@C/CNTs synthesized through a spray drying method are composed of micron-sized primary particles dispersed within the intertwined carbon nanotube matrix.  The CNT framework not only provides an efficient elec. highway between primary particles, but also forms a stable mech. backbone for secondary particles.  The initial discharge capacity of NVPF@C/CNTs is about 113 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1C, and the cell retains 98.2% after 300 cycles.  Besides, a high rate capacity of 85 mA h g-1 has been achieved at 30C.  We believe that our work presented here will be favorable for accelerating the commercialization of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.ssi.2006.07.028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gover, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The structural and alkali-ion insertion characteristics of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 are presented.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is a pos. electrode material for Na-ion batteries which is attracting strong interest due to its high capacity, rate capability, and long-term cycling stability.  The sodium extn. mechanism from this material was always described in the literature as a straightforward solid soln., but several hints point toward a more complicated phase diagram.  In this work we performed high angular resoln. synchrotron radiation diffraction measurements, realized operando on sodium batteries upon charge.  We reveal an extremely interesting phase diagram, created by the successive crystn. of four intermediate phases before the end compn. NaV2(PO4)2F3 is reached.  Only one of these phases undergoes a solid soln. reaction, in the interval between 1.8 and 1.3 Na per formula unit.  The ability to resolve weak Bragg reflections allowed us to reveal differences in terms of symmetry among the phases, to det. their previously unknown space groups, and to correlate them with sodium (dis)ordering in the structure.  Rietveld refinements enabled us to follow fine structural modifications in great detail.  Intermediate identified phases are not simply described by their unit cell parameters, but bond-length variations can be tracked, as well as polyhedral distortions and site occupancy factors for mobile sodium ions.  For NaV2(PO4)2F3 a full crystal structure detn. was also carried out for the first time directly from operando measurements, assigning it to the Cmc21 space group and revealing two vanadium environments: V3+ and V5+.  Our study demonstrates that improved angular resoln. and high intensity diffraction data are key parameters for direct observation of fine reaction pathways in electrode materials and that the obtained insight is crucial for the understanding of (de)intercalation mechanisms in Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1039/C1EE01263K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding and recent development of carbon coating on LiFePO<sub>4</sub> cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Olivine-structured LiFePO4 has been the focus of research in developing low cost, high performance cathode materials for lithium ion batteries.  Various processes have been developed to synthesize LiFePO4 or C/LiFePO4 (carbon coating on LiFePO4), and some of them are being used to mass produce C/LiFePO4 at the com. or pilot scale.  Due to the low intrinsic electronic and ionic conductivities of LiFePO4, the decrease of particle size and the nano-layer of carbon coating on LiFePO4 particle surfaces are necessary to achieve a high electrochem. performance.  Significant progress has been made in understanding and controlling phase purity, particle size and carbon coating of the C/LiFePO4 composite material in the past.  However, there are still many challenges in achieving a high quality product with high consistency.  In this review, we summarize some of the recent progress and advances based on selected reports from peer-reviewed journal publications.
